        <meta property="og:url" content="https://pubs.acs.org/doi/full/10.1021/acsami.9b22745"><meta property="og:title" content="Hyperaccumulation Route to Ca-Rich Hard Carbon Materials with Cation Self-Incorporation and Interlayer Spacing Optimization for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries"><meta property="og:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b22745/asset/images/acsami.9b22745.social.jpeg_v03"><meta property="og:description" content="The hard carbon (HC) has been emerging as one of the most promising anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs). Incorporation of cations into the HC lattice proved to be effective to regulate their d-interlayer spacing with a modified SIB performance. However, the complexity and high cost of current synthetic processes limited its large-scale application in SIBs. Through the natural hyperaccumulation process, a cost-effective and scale-up-driven procedure to produce Ca-ion self-incorporated HC materials was proposed by applying tamarind fruits as the precursor with the enrichment of Ca ions. In virtue of one-step pyrolysis, the self-incorporated and well-distributed Ca ions in tamarind fruits had successfully served as the buffer layer to expand the d-interlayer spacing of HC materials. Furthermore, the natural porosity hierarchy could be largely preserved by the optimization of calcination temperature. As a result, the Ca-rich HC material had exhibited the optimized cycling performance (326.7 mA h g–1 at 50 mA g–1 and capacity retention rate of 89.40% after 250 cycles) with a high initial Coulombic efficiency of 70.39%. This work provided insight into applying the hyperaccumulation effect of biomass precursors to produce doped HC materials with ion self-incorporation and the optimized d-interlayer spacing, navigating its large-scale application for high-performance SIBs."><meta property="og:type" content="Article"><meta property="og:site_name" content="ACS Publications"><meta name="twitter:card" content="summary_large_image"><meta name="twitter:site" content="@ACSPublications"><meta name="twitter:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b22745/asset/images/acsami.9b22745.social.jpeg_v03">

<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/wro/1122814~thiss-ds.js" async="" nonce="93188b05780c075e-SJC"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="93188b05780c075e-SJC">

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            timeout: 5000,

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
            },
            retrieveEntity: function (ms) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                if (ms == undefined || ms === '') {
                    ms = this.timeout;
                }

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res.data);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('failed to retrieve entity from local storage: ' + err);
                        });
                    // Set up the timeout
                    setTimeout(function () {
                        reject('Promise timed out ' + ms + ' ms');
                    }, ms);
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage due to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {
                            doi: doi,
                            entityid: entityId,
                            entityTitle: entityTitle,
                            eventGroupKey: 'f5c233cc-f65b-4391-9878-141464e531de'
                        }

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    }).fail(function (status) {
                        return reject(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (i = 0; i < allSsoInstitutions.length; i++) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        if(allSsoInstitutions.length === 0 && true){
                            self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, null, null)
                                .then(function () {
                                    console.log('No Entity found');
                                }, function (err) {
                                    console.log('failed to get the none entity status' ,err);
                                });
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            }).catch(function (err) {
                                reject(err);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();

                    if ($('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').length > 0) {
                        let institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox = $('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').get(0);
                        if (!$(institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox).is(":checked")) {
                            return;
                        }
                    }

                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="93188b05780c075e-SJC">
var dfpReady = false;
$(document).ready(function() {
    // var journalTitle = 'applied_materials_interfaces';
    var taxonomyKeywords = $('.article_header-taxonomy');
    var articleKeyword = $('meta[name="keywords"]');
    var articleTitle = $('meta[name="dc.Title"]');
    var articleDescription = $('meta[name="dc.Description"]');
    var abstractKeyword = $('p.articleBody_abstractText:contains("Keywords: ")');
    var searchTerms = [];

    if (taxonomyKeywords.length > 0) {
        $(taxonomyKeywords).children(".rlist--inline").children("li").each(function() {
            searchTerms.push($(this).text());
        });
    }
    else if (articleKeyword.length > 0) { 
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleKeyword.prop('content').split(', '));
    }
    else if (abstractKeyword.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(abstractKeyword.text().split("Keywords: ")[1].split('; '));
    }
    else if (articleDescription.length > 0) {
        $(articleDescription).each(function() {
            articleDescriptionKeywords = $(this).prop('content');
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/.,/g,"");
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/\s{2,}/g," ");
            searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleDescriptionKeywords.split(' '));
        });
    }

    if (articleTitle.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleTitle.prop('content').split(' '));
    }

    googletag.cmd.push(function() {
        var mappingLeader = googletag.sizeMapping().
        addSize([750, 200], [728, 90]). 
        addSize([0, 0], [320, 50]).
        build();
        //leaderboard
        googletag.defineSlot('/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article', [728, 90], 'dfp-journal-article-leaderboard').defineSizeMapping(mappingLeader).setTargeting('location', 'leaderboard1').setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //recommend
        googletag.defineSlot("/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article", [1, 1], "dfp-journal-article-recommend").setTargeting("ntvPlacement", ["1100167"]).setTargeting("location", "recommend").setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //googletag.pubads().enableSingleRequest();
        googletag.pubads().collapseEmptyDivs();
        googletag.pubads().setTargeting('inst',dartInstitutionType).setTargeting('memb',dartMember);
        googletag.pubads().addEventListener("slotRenderEnded", function(event) {
            console.log(event.slot.getSlotElementId() + " isEmpty: " + event.isEmpty + " | creative id: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            if((event.isEmpty === false) && (event.slot.getSlotElementId() != "dfp-journal-article-recommend")) {
                $("#" + event.slot.getSlotElementId()).parents(".advertisement").slideDown();
                console.log("ad display: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            }
            // else {
            //     console.log("no ad found");
            // }
        });
        googletag.enableServices();
        dfpReady = true;
    });
});
</script>

data-getftr-references-enabled="data-getFTR-references-enabled" data-getftr-reference-url="/action/CitationEntitlement" data-getftr-citedby-enabled="data-getFTR-citedBy-enabled" class="article--latest"><div class="figure-viewer"><div class="figure-viewer_row"><div class="figure-viewer_col loop-trap"><div aria-live="polite" aria-atomic="true" class="figure-viewer_modal"><a class="figure-viewer_image"><a href="#" title="Next" class="figure-viewer_next icon-angle-right"></a><a href="#" title="Previous" class="figure-viewer_prev icon-angle-left"></a><div class="figure-viewer_image-content"><img src="" alt="Figure 1" class="fv-img"><img src="/specs/products/achs/releasedAssets/images/loading/loading-018624cffd023ad5641b8e99931a80e6.gif" alt="Loading href="/action/showCitFormats?doi=10.1021/acsami.9b22745&amp;href=/doi/10.1021/acsami.9b22745" title="Cite This" class="figure-viewer-cite-this-link"><i class="icon-check-circle"></i><span><strong>Cite <script nonce="93188b05780c075e-SJC">
$(function() {
    var serialCode = "aamick";
    var books = ["reagents", "symposium", "advances", "medichemreviews", "styleguide"]
    if(books.includes(serialCode) === false) {
        // default click action
        $("[data-id]").on("mousedown", function(e) {
            var currentClickID = $(this).attr("data-id");

            if(currentClickID.includes("_hover") === false) {
                if(currentClickID.match("^article_") && !currentClickID.match("^article_abstract_CC")) {   
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Hyperaccumulation Route to Ca-Rich Hard Carbon Materials with Cation Self-Incorporation and Interlayer Spacing Optimization for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.9b22745", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                }
            }
        });
        
        // Access Management icons hover
        var articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        var articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent === false) {
                articleAccessManagementIconHover = true;
                var articleAccessManagementHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleAccessManagementIconHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Hyperaccumulation Route to Ca-Rich Hard Carbon Materials with Cation Self-Incorporation and Interlayer Spacing Optimization for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.9b22745", "Article_Element": articleAccessManagementHover });
    
                        articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        });
    
        // articleRightsPermissionsLink hover
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent === false) {
                articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = true;
                var articleRightsHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Hyperaccumulation Route to Ca-Rich Hard Carbon Materials with Cation Self-Incorporation and Interlayer Spacing Optimization for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.9b22745", "Article_Element": articleRightsHover });
    
                        articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        });
    
        // Author hover
        var articleAuthorHover = false
        var articleAuthorHoverEvent = false
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if((articleAuthorHoverEvent === false) && ($(this).parent().hasClass("view-affs") === false)) {
                articleAuthorHover = true;
                var authorInfoHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAuthorHover === true) && (articleAuthorHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Hyperaccumulation Route to Ca-Rich Hard Carbon Materials with Cation Self-Incorporation and Interlayer Spacing Optimization for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.9b22745", "Article_Element": authorInfoHover });
    
                        articleAuthorHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAuthorHover = false;
        });
    
        // CC License hover
        var articleAbstractCCHover = false
        var articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = false
        var articleDrawerCCHover = false
        var articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = false
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if($(this).attr("data-id")) {
                if(($(this).attr("data-id") === "article_drawer_CC-License") && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleDrawerCCHover = true;
                    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleDrawerCCHover === true) && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Hyperaccumulation Route to Ca-Rich Hard Carbon Materials with Cation Self-Incorporation and Interlayer Spacing Optimization for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.9b22745", "Article_Element": "article_drawer_CC-License_hover" });
    
                            articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
                else if(($(this).attr("data-id").match("^article_abstract_CC")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleAbstractCCHover = true;
    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Hyperaccumulation Route to Ca-Rich Hard Carbon Materials with Cation Self-Incorporation and Interlayer Spacing Optimization for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.9b22745", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                            articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
            }
            else if(($(this).hasClass("article__cc-license__link")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = true;
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Hyperaccumulation Route to Ca-Rich Hard Carbon Materials with Cation Self-Incorporation and Interlayer Spacing Optimization for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.9b22745", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                        articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            if(articleAbstractCCHover === true) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = false;
            }
            if(articleDrawerCCHover = true) {
                articleDrawerCCHover = false;
            }
        });
        
        // show recommeneded click delay
        var intervalCount = 0;
        var showRecommendedInterval = setInterval(function() {
            intervalCount += 100;
            if($(".show-recommended__wrapper .show-recommended").length > 0) {
                clearInterval(showRecommendedInterval);
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowMore']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Hyperaccumulation Route to Ca-Rich Hard Carbon Materials with Cation Self-Incorporation and Interlayer Spacing Optimization for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.9b22745", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowLess']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Hyperaccumulation Route to Ca-Rich Hard Carbon Materials with Cation Self-Incorporation and Interlayer Spacing Optimization for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.9b22745", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
            }
        }, 100);
    }
});
</script>

Technology, Beijing 100081, PR China</div></div><div class="loa-info-scifinder"><span>More by <a href="/action/doSearch?field1=Contrib&amp;text1=Kaihua++Yu" data-id="article_author_search">Kaihua href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D10544%26pageCount%3D10%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DKaihua%2BYu%252C%2BHuichun%2BZhao%252C%2BXinran%2BWang%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D12%26issueNum%3D9%26contentID%3Dacsami.9b22745%26title%3DHyperaccumulation%2BRoute%2Bto%2BCa-Rich%2BHard%2BCarbon%2BMaterials%2Bwith%2BCation%2BSelf-Incorporation%2Band%2BInterlayer%2BSpacing%2BOptimization%2Bfor%2BHigh-Performance%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26numPages%3D10%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1944-8244%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Daamick%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D10553%26publicationDate%3DMarch%2B2020" data-id="article_rights_permissions">Request reuse permissions</a></div></div></div></div></div><div class="article_header-metrics-dropzone" data-pb-dropzone="article_header-metrics-dropzone"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div></div></div></div><div class="article_abstract"><div class="article_abstract-title" id="Abstract" tabindex="0"><h2>Abstract</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div><div class="article_abstract-content hlFld-Abstract" id="abstractBox" property="description"><figure id="_i1" data-index="0" class="article__inlineFigure article_abstract-img"><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img class="inline-fig internalNav" src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b22745/asset/images/medium/am9b22745_0008.gif" alt="" id="tgr1" property="image" style="width:405px; height:275px"></button><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b22745/asset/images/large/am9b22745_0008.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.9b22745&amp;id=_i1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p class="articleBody_abstractText">The hard carbon (HC) has been emerging as one of the most promising anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs). Incorporation of cations into the HC lattice proved to be effective to regulate their <i>d</i>-interlayer spacing with a modified SIB performance. However, the complexity and high cost of current synthetic processes limited its large-scale application in SIBs. Through the natural hyperaccumulation process, a cost-effective and scale-up-driven procedure to produce Ca-ion self-incorporated HC materials was proposed by applying tamarind fruits as the precursor with the enrichment of Ca ions. In virtue of one-step pyrolysis, the self-incorporated and well-distributed Ca ions in tamarind fruits had successfully served as the buffer layer to expand the <i>d</i>-interlayer spacing of HC materials. Furthermore, the natural porosity hierarchy could be largely preserved by the optimization of calcination temperature. As a result, the Ca-rich HC material had exhibited the optimized cycling performance (326.7 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at 50 mA g<sup>–1</sup> and capacity retention rate of 89.40% after 250 cycles) with a high initial Coulombic efficiency of 70.39%. This work provided insight into applying the hyperaccumulation effect of biomass precursors to produce doped HC materials with ion self-incorporation and the optimized <i>d</i>-interlayer spacing, navigating its large-scale application for high-performance SIBs.</p></div><div class="article__cc-license"><div class="article__cc-license__body"><p class="article__cc-license__para">This publication is licensed under the terms of your
                            institutional subscription.
                            <a href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D10544%26pageCount%3D10%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DKaihua%2BYu%252C%2BHuichun%2BZhao%252C%2BXinran%2BWang%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D12%26issueNum%3D9%26contentID%3Dacsami.9b22745%26title%3DHyperaccumulation%2BRoute%2Bto%2BCa-Rich%2BHard%2BCarbon%2BMaterials%2Bwith%2BCation%2BSelf-Incorporation%2Band%2BInterlayer%2BSpacing%2BOptimization%2Bfor%2BHigh-Performance%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26numPages%3D10%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1944-8244%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Daamick%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D10553%26publicationDate%3DMarch%2B2020" class="link--bold">Request reuse permissions.</a></p></div></div><span class="hidden" property="publisher">ACS Publications</span><div class="article_header-article-copyright">Copyright © 2020 American Chemical Society</div><div class="article_header-footer-right"><div class="articleHeaderDropzone7" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone7"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div><div class="article__tags article__tags--subjects"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Subjects</h3><div tabindex="0" class="article__tags__tooltip"><div aria-describedby="tooltip-subjects" class="article__tags__icon"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are subjects</span></div><p id="tooltip-subjects" role="tooltip" class="article__tags__diff">
                                        Article subjects are automatically applied from the ACS Subject Taxonomy and describe the scientific concepts and themes of the article.</p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291356&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Defects"> Defects </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=290667&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Ions"> Ions </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291146&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Lattices"> Lattices </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=292506&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Materials"> Materials </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291087&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Precursors"> Precursors </a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="article__tags article__tags--keywords hlFld-Abstract"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Keywords</h3><div class="article__tags__tooltip" tabindex="0"><div class="article__tags__icon" aria-describedby="tooltip-keywords"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are keywords</span></div><p class="article__tags__diff" id="tooltip-keywords" role="tooltip">
                        Article keywords are supplied by the authors and highlight key terms and topics
                        of the paper.
                    </p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Sodium-ion+Batteries&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_sodium-ion%20batteries">sodium-ion batteries</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Hard+Carbon&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_hard%20carbon">hard carbon</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Anode&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_anode">anode</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Tamarind&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_tamarind">tamarind</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Hyperaccumulation&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_hyperaccumulation">hyperaccumulation</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="article_content"><div class="article_content-table hlFld-FullText"><div class="article_content-row"><div class="article_content-left" property="articleBody"><div id="sec1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i2">1.  Introduction</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">Although the renewable energy has been in active exploration in recent years, its utilization remains a challenge due to the intermittent conveying and the uneven distribution. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1 ref2 ref3" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref1 ref2 ref3" aria-label="reference 1 to 3">(1−3)</a> As a result, several of advanced energy conversion and storage devices have been continuously developed to address the challenge. In this regard, lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) have become the most promising and attractive choice for portable electric devices and storage devices. However, the insufficient Li resources can hardly cover the ever-growing demand of LIBs in particular with the demanded large-scale storage devices in future. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref2 ref3 ref4" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref2 ref3 ref4" aria-label="reference 2 to 4">(2−4)</a> Alternatively, sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are recently attracting the tremendous attention on the large-scale energy storage on account of their abundance of Na, low-cost, environmental-friendliness, and the similarity between Li and Na. Therefore, it is essential to develop the corresponding electrode materials of low cost and renewability, while fulfilling the large-scale applicable requirements arising from the boom of electrical vehicles and stationary energy systems. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref3 ref4 ref5 ref6" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref3 ref4 ref5 ref6" aria-label="reference 3 to 6">(3−6)</a></div><div class="NLM_p">According to the literature, a great deal of materials have been studied as anode candidates, including carbon materials, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref7 ref8 ref9" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref7 ref8 ref9" aria-label="reference 7 to 9">(7−9)</a> sulfides, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref10 ref11 ref12" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref10 ref11 ref12" aria-label="reference 10 to 12">(10−12)</a> metal oxides, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref13 ref14 ref15" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref13 ref14 ref15" aria-label="reference 13 to 15">(13−15)</a> alloys, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref16 ref17 ref18" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref16 ref17 ref18" aria-label="reference 16 to 18">(16−18)</a> and so forth. To date, the hard carbon (HC) material is still identified as the most promising and industry-accessible anode because of its large <i>d</i>-interlayer spacing for Na ion insertion, low average potential of sodiation/desodiation, and the most cost-effectiveness, which is the top priority for the industrialization of SIBs. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref19" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref19" aria-label="reference 19">(19)</a> Owing to the advantages of being low-cost, renewable, and environmentally friendly, the biomass has showed great promises as precursors to produce HC materials, while minimizing the wastes caused by the current handling of incineration or landfill. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref20" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref20" aria-label="reference 20">(20)</a> Accordingly, many recent researches have reported the biomass-derived HC materials with the capacity generally ranging from 240 to ∼310 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at the current density of 50 mA g<sup>–1</sup>. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref21 ref22 ref23" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref21 ref22 ref23" aria-label="reference 21 to 23">(21−23)</a> More recent studies on the charge-transfer mechanism shows that the low voltage part (0.0–0.1 V) corresponds to Na ions embedded in the carbon layers while the high-voltage range (0.1–2 V) is related to the reaction of Na ions on the surface of the carbon material. There is no uniform conclusion on the mechanism of sodium storage in HC materials. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref24" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref24" aria-label="reference 24">(24)</a> In this regard, the <i>d</i>-interlayer spacing of HC materials proves to be important on their electrochemical performance when accommodated with Na ions, and the <i>d</i>-interlayer spacing varies significantly with the species of precursors and post-treatment temperature. The Na ion can undergo electrochemical insertion/extraction when the <i>d</i>-interlayer spacing exceeds 0.37 nm. It indicates that a larger <i>d</i>-interlayer spacing facilitates the Na-ion insertion/extraction to enhance the electrochemical performance, which has also been proved by Cao through experimental and theoretical calculations. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref24" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref24" aria-label="reference 24">(24)</a> Kelp-derived HC materials presented a wide range of <i>d</i>-interlayer spacing from 3.9 to 4.3 Å by changing the calcination temperature. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref3" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref3" aria-label="reference 3">(3)</a> Another work on mangosteen shell-derived HC materials has suggested that calcining at 1500 °C gave rise to an optimal reversible capacity of ∼330 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at 30 mA g<sup>–1</sup> with the initial Coulombic efficiency (ICE) of ∼83%. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref25" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref25" aria-label="reference 25">(25)</a> In order to attain larger <i>d</i>-interlayer spacing, the procedure of heterogeneous cation occupation has been proposed widespread, where selected ions have been intentionally incorporated into HC materials. These heterogeneous atoms can uptake certain volume during the graphitization process and, therefore, engage to regulate the <i>d</i>-interlayer spacing. However, the most of investigations requires exogenous salts for introducing the heterogeneous atoms as well as the additional process for its homogenization with biomass precursors. In addition, it is challenging to intensively distribute heterogeneous atoms into the biomass structure. On the contrary, inspired by the hyperaccumulation of plants, several of ions can be selectively enriched and dispersed uniformly into plant tissues. The enriched cations could serve as a natural self-incorporated heterogeneous atom for the synthesis of doped HC materials. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref26" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref26" aria-label="reference 26">(26)</a> The enrichment effect of plants is a biological phenomenon widely existing in natural plants. Natural plants have complex and exquisite microstructures, and these structures ensure transport stability while serving for nutrition transfer. Based on these cases, plants can selectively absorb certain required substances from the environment to rhizomes and transfer them to specific parts. During the whole process, some specific metal ions, such as Ca ions, K ions, Zn ions, and so forth, will also be absorbed and enriched in certain parts of plants. In this regard, the tamarind is a green economic plant widely cultivated in tropical and subtropical regions for the major use of nutrition, medicine, and ornament. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref22" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref22" aria-label="reference 22">(22)</a> Many parts of tamarind, such as the extracts of leaves, flesh, seed, and root bark, have been recorded to have positive antibacterial, anti-inflammatory, anti-drug, analgesic, hypoglycemic, and hypolipidemic effects. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref26 ref27" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref26 ref27" aria-label="reference 26 and 27">(26,27)</a> In particular, tamarinds can enrich Ca ions naturally, being potentially a self-incorporated precursor to regulate the <i>d</i>-interlayer spacing. Unfortunately, to the best of our knowledge, it is unprecedented to use the tamarind fruit as precursor to produce HC materials rather than their performance optimization for SIBs.</div><div class="NLM_p last">Herein, we have applied the tamarind fruit shell as biomass precursors to produce HC materials, where a cost-effective, facile, and straight forward pyrolysis procedure was introduced. The relationship between the lattice structure and electrochemical properties of HC was revealed as varying the calcination temperature. In particular, the HC material prepared at 1200 °C exhibited the optimal electrochemical performances due to the balance among the <i>d</i>-interlayer spacing, graphitization and defects, and nanoporosity in the microstructure. Moreover, the hyperaccumulation effect of Ca ions has been identified and confirmed to further expand the <i>d</i>-interlayer spacing and facilitate the Na-ion transport in the insertion/extraction processes. As a result, a reversible capacity of 326.7 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> was achieved at the current density of 50 mA g<sup>–1</sup> with the capacity retention of 89.4% after 250 cycles.</div></div><div id="sec2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i3">2.  Experimental Section</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div id="sec2_1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i4" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i4">2.1.  Synthesis of Ca-Rich HC Materials</h3><div class="NLM_p last">The tamarind was purchased from Yunnan province, China. Before calcination, the tamarind shell was washed with the deionized water several times. The tamarind shell was then cut into pieces, smashed, and dried at 80 °C for 24 h. Consequently, the dried powder was loaded into a tubular furnace and carbonized at certain temperature with a heating rate of 5 °C min<sup>–1</sup> under Ar flow. By varying the calcination temperature (800, 1000, 1100, 1200, and 1300 °C), different HC samples were obtained and thereafter noted as HC-800, HC-1000, HC-1200, and HC-1300, respectively. After cooling down to room temperature naturally, the prepared HC materials were collected for the following tests. Particularly, the HC-1200 sample was then washed again with 0.5 M HCl for 6 h to remove the residue Ca ions. The sample was dried at 120 °C overnight in vacuum (noted as HC-1200H).</div></div><div id="sec2_2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i5" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i5">2.2.  Material Characterization</h3><div class="NLM_p last">The morphology and crystalline characteristics of the Ca-rich HC were analyzed by using the scanning electron microscope (SEM, Zeiss Supra 55/3195) and transmission electron microscopy (HR-TEM, JEOL JEM-ARM200CF). The crystallographic characteristics were examined by using a X-ray diffractometer (XRD, D/MAX-RB) with Cu Kα radiation and X-ray wavelength of 1.5418 Å. Raman analyses were performed with a Renishaw visual Raman microscope by using a 514 nm laser beam with a spectral resolution of 1 cm<sup>–1</sup>. The mesoporous structure and the elemental composition were characterized by a CO<sub>2</sub> and N<sub>2</sub> sorption Brunauer–Emmett–Teller (BET, ASAP 2020 HD88 Quantachrome instrument) measurement, X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS, PHI5700) and an inductively coupled plasma optical emission spectrometry (ICP-OES, Optima 8300).</div></div><div id="sec2_3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i6" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i6">2.3.  Electrochemical Measurements</h3><div class="NLM_p last">The electrochemical performance of HC materials was evaluated by using 2025-type coin-cells assembled in an argon-filled glove box (MBRAUN-6020 with the content of water and oxygen less than 0.1 ppm). The working electrodes were prepared by pasting mixture slurry of active materials, carbon black, and poly(vinylidene fluoride) (PVDF) onto a copper foil with a weight ratio of 8:1:1. The slurry was then dried at 120 °C overnight under vacuum. The Na metal was used as a counter electrode with the glass fiber as the separator. 1 M NaClO<sub>4</sub> dissolved in 1 L propylene carbonate (PC) with (5 vol %) fluoroethylene carbonate was applied as the electrolyte. The cyclic voltammetry (CV) measurements were carried out by using an electrochemical workstation (CHI660E) from 0.1 to 2.5 V at a scan rate of 0.1 mV s<sup>–1</sup>. Electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) measurements were also performed on the same electrochemical workstation with the frequency ranged from 100 kHz to 0.01 Hz. The charge/discharge measurements were performed by using a Land-CT2011A battery tester between 0.01 and 2.50 V.</div></div></div><div id="sec3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i7">3.  Results and Discussion</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">The Ca-incorporated HC samples present a similar structural hierarchy when varying the calcination temperature from 800 to 1300 °C (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a> inset). However, as suggested by the HR-TEM images (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>), the crystal structure of these HC samples shows obvious changes due to the graphitization. The ordering of the short-range lattice structure indicates the local turbostratic characteristics for the typical HC materials. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref24 ref29" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref24 ref29" aria-label="reference 24 and 29">(24,29)</a> Accompanied by the increase of calcination temperature (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>a–e), the detailed TEM images indicates the reduction of the <i>d</i>-interlayer spacing from ∼0.42 to ∼0.38 nm. The changes of <i>d</i>-interlayer spacing are mainly compared in <a class="ref showTableEvent internalNav" data-id="tbl1" href="#tbl1">Tables </a><a class="ref showTableEvent internalNav" data-id="tbl1" href="#tbl1">1</a> and <a class="ref showTableEvent internalNav" data-id="tbl2" href="#tbl2">2</a>. Apparently, raising the calcination temperature promotes the pyrolysis process, generating the relatively higher degree of graphitization with more narrowed <i>d</i>-interlayer spacing. Furthermore, the tamarind fruit is particularly selected in this study as the natural Ca-rich precursor due to the hyperaccumulation phenomenon and these metal cations are dispersed uniformly into tamarind tissues. During the pyrolysis process, these metal ions are considered to extend the <i>d</i>-interlayer spacing as the resulting HC materials generally hold a larger <i>d</i>-interlayer spacing than other HC cases reported elsewhere. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref30 ref31 ref32 ref33 ref34" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref30 ref31 ref32 ref33 ref34" aria-label="reference 30 to 34">(30−34)</a> As a result, we compare the morphology and lattice characteristics of the HC-1200 sample before and after the removal of Ca ions. By <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>a,b inset, no obvious change has been suggested on their morphology, confirming no major structural change. Therefore, it suggests that the Ca ion occupies between interlayers. Here, we indeed observe the significantly reduced <i>d</i>-interlayer spacing from ∼0.40 to ∼0.38 nm (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>d,f) by removing metal cations (HC-1200H). <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref32 ref33 ref34 ref35 ref36" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref32 ref33 ref34 ref35 ref36" aria-label="reference 32 to 36">(32−36)</a> Besides, the corresponding selected area electron diffraction (SAED) pattern inset suggests the typical polycrystalline characteristics of HC materials due to the presence of local turbostratic structures. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref30 ref31 ref37 ref38" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref30 ref31 ref37 ref38" aria-label="reference 30, 31, 37 and 38">(30,31,37,38)</a> The SAED patterns become sharper by increasing the temperature, which indicates the trend of the lattice graphitization. In order to further examine the residue Ca ions in lattice, the EDS elemental mappings were conducted and shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>. Compared with <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>a,b, the surface of HC materials is rather smooth without any observable aggregation particles. The EDS analysis on these regions further reveals the presence of the Ca ion, K ion, and Cl ion, which are well distributed in HC materials. These uniform cations further indicate that they are located between interlayers instead of aggregations on the surface. In addition, the acid-washing engages to remove the most of ions in HC materials in the lattice. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref30 ref31" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref30 ref31" aria-label="reference 30 and 31">(30,31)</a></div><figure id="fig1" data-index="1" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 1</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b22745/asset/images/medium/am9b22745_0001.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b22745/asset/images/large/am9b22745_0001.jpeg" id="gr1" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 1. HR-TEM images of the hard carbon prepared at different calcination temperature: (a) HC-800, (b) HC-1000, (c) HC-1100, (d) HC-1200, (e) HC-1300, and (f) HC-1200H. The insets of (a–f) show the SAED patterns (upper right corner) and SEM (lower left corner) of corresponding samples.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b22745/asset/images/large/am9b22745_0001.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.9b22745&amp;id=fig1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><figure id="fig2" data-index="2" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 2</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b22745/asset/images/medium/am9b22745_0002.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b22745/asset/images/large/am9b22745_0002.jpeg" id="gr2" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 2.
